{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01LoFs2zm5sHGDr4eR7u8Wfq","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"So here's the flow:\n1. `nfs_lookup_revalidate` calls `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` (line 1158)\n2. `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` calls `__nfs_revalidate_inode` (line 1073)\n3. This calls `nfs_zap_caches(dir)` (line 1213) which zaps the parent directory cache\n5. And then goes to `out_bad` which returns 0, marking the dentry as invalid\n\nThe bug is that when `__nfs_revalidate_inode` returns -512 (ERESTARTSYS), this is treated as an error and the parent directory is zapped and the dentry is marked invalid. \n\nBut -512/ERESTARTSYS is not a real error - it means a signal was received and the system call should be restarted. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_013W8J7f2D7PzWCkKF8E763u","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"BINGO! I found it! The bug is in `nfs3_rpc_wrapper` function at lines 30-42 in `fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c`.\n\nThe problem is:\n1. `rpc_call_sync` is called and returns `res`\n2. If `res != -EJUKEBOX`, it breaks out of the loop\n3. But if `res` is `0` (success) or any other error code, it checks `while (!fatal_signal_pending(current))`\n4. The issue is at line 39: `res = -ERESTARTSYS;` is set BEFORE checking the fatal signal condition!\n\nThe logic is:\n```c\ndo {\n    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);  // This could return 0 (success) or -512 or any error\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n        break;  // If not EJUKEBOX, exit the loop\n    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n    res = -ERESTARTSYS;  // This sets res to -ERESTARTSYS\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n```\n\nWait, let me re-read this more carefully. The loop breaks if `res != -EJUKEBOX`. So:\n- If `rpc_call_sync` returns 0 (success), it breaks and returns 0\n- If `rpc_call_sync` returns -EJUKEBOX, it continues the loop\n- After the sleep, it sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS` and checks the while condition\n\nActually, the logic seems correct for handling EJUKEBOX (which is a special NFS error meaning \"try again\"). But let me check if this wrapper is used for all NFS3 procedures...\n\nThe problem is that this wrapper is defined at the top of nfs3proc.c and there's a #define at line 44:\n\n\n```c\n#define rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags)\tnfs3_rpc_wrapper(clnt, msg, flags)\n```\n\nThis macro replaces every `rpc_call_sync` call in the file with the wrapper, meaning all NFS3 RPC calls go through this retry logic. The issue is that when `rpc_call_sync` returns anything other than -EJUKEBOX, the loop exits immediately, but the wrapper still overwrites the result with -ERESTARTSYS if a signal arrives during the sleep phase. This causes successful operations to be incorrectly reported as interrupted. Looking at the loop structure more carefully: if the RPC call succeeds initially, we break immediately and return 0. If it returns -EJUKEBOX, we sleep and retry. In order to catch any callbacks that\n     * clean up after sleeping on some queue, we don't\n     * break the loop here, but go around once more.\n     */\n    dprintk(\"RPC: %5u got signal\\n\", task->tk_pid);\n    task->tk_flags |= RPC_TASK_KILLED;\n    rpc_exit(task, -ERESTARTSYS);\n}\n```\n\nSo when `out_of_line_wait_on_bit` returns `-ERESTARTSYS` (because a signal was pending), the task is exited with `-ERESTARTSYS` status! This is the problem!\n\nThe issue is that `out_of_line_wait_on_bit` with `rpc_wait_bit_killable` is returning -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC task has actually completed! When an RPC response arrives from the server while the sync task is waiting on RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit and a signal arrives, the out_of_line_wait_on_bit call returns -ERESTARTSYS.
